<p><b>Maine</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>) is the northernmost <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> region of the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">northeastern United States</a>. Maine is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area" title="List of U.S. states and territories by area">39th most extensive</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population">41st most populous</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states" title="List of U.S. states">U.S. states</a> and <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States" title="Territories of the United States">territories</a>. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a> to the west, the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to the southeast, and the <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">Canadian provinces</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> to the northeast and northwest respectively. Maine is the easternmost state in the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">contiguous United States</a>, and the northernmost east of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a>. It is known for its jagged, rocky coastline; low, rolling mountains; heavily forested interior, and picturesque waterways; and also its seafood cuisine, especially <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clams" title="Clams">clams</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_lobster" title="American lobster">lobster</a>. There is a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> throughout the state, even in coastal areas such as its most populous city of <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Maine" title="Portland, Maine">Portland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The capital is <a href="/wiki/Augusta,_Maine" title="Augusta, Maine">Augusta</a>.</p>
<p>For thousands of years, <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">indigenous peoples</a> were the only inhabitants of the territory that is now Maine. At the time of European arrival in what is now Maine, several <a href="/wiki/Algonquian_languages" title="Algonquian languages">Algonquian</a>-speaking peoples inhabited the area. The first European settlement in the area was by the French in 1604 on <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix_Island,_Maine" title="Saint Croix Island, Maine">Saint Croix Island</a>, by <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Dugua,_Sieur_de_Mons" title="Pierre Dugua, Sieur de Mons">Pierre Dugua, Sieur de Mons</a>. The first English settlement was the short-lived <a href="/wiki/Popham_Colony" title="Popham Colony">Popham Colony</a>, established by the <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Company" title="Plymouth Company">Plymouth Company</a> in 1607. A number of English settlements were established along the coast of Maine in the 1620s, although the rugged climate, deprivations, and conflict with the local peoples caused many to fail over the years.</p>
<p>As Maine entered the 18th century, only a half dozen European settlements had survived. <a href="/wiki/Loyalist_(American_Revolution)" title="Loyalist (American Revolution)">Loyalist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patriot_(American_Revolution)" title="Patriot (American Revolution)">Patriot</a> forces contended for Maine's territory during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a> and the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>. At the close of the War of 1812, it was occupied by British forces, but the territory of Maine was returned to the United States as part of a peace treaty that was to include dedicated land on the Michigan peninsula for Native American peoples. Maine was part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Massachusetts" title="Commonwealth of Massachusetts">Commonwealth of Massachusetts</a> until 1820, when it voted to secede from Massachusetts to become a separate state. On March 15, 1820, under the <a href="/wiki/Missouri_Compromise" title="Missouri Compromise">Missouri Compromise</a>, it was <a href="/wiki/Admission_to_the_Union" title="Admission to the Union">admitted to the Union</a> as the 23rd state.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There is no definitive explanation for the origin of the name "Maine", but the most likely origin is that the name was given by early explorers after the province of <a href="/wiki/Maine_(province)" title="Maine (province)">Maine</a> in France. Whatever the origin, the name was fixed for English settlers in 1665 when the English King's Commissioners ordered that the "Province of Maine" be entered from then on in official records.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stewart_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stewart-11">[11]</a></sup> The state legislature in 2001 adopted a resolution establishing Franco-American Day, which stated that the state was named after the former <a href="/wiki/Maine_(province)" title="Maine (province)">French province of Maine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Other theories mention earlier places with similar names, or claim it is a nautical reference to the mainland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Attempts to uncover the history of the name of Maine began with James Sullivan's 1795 "History of the District of Maine". He made the unsubstantiated allegation that the Province of Maine was a compliment to the queen of <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henrietta_Maria" title="Henrietta Maria">Henrietta Maria</a>, who once "owned" the Province of Maine in France. This was quoted by Maine historians until the 1845 biography of that queen by Agnes Strickland<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> established that she had no connection to the Province of Maine in France; further, King Charles I married Henrietta Maria in 1625, three years after the name Maine first appeared on the charter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fisher2002_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fisher2002-15">[15]</a></sup> A new theory, put forward by Carol B. Smith Fisher in 2002, is that <a href="/wiki/Ferdinando_Gorges" title="Ferdinando Gorges">Sir Ferdinando Gorges</a> chose the name in 1622 to honor the village where his ancestors first lived in England, rather than the province in France. "MAINE" appears in the <a href="/wiki/Domesday_Book" title="Domesday Book">Domesday Book</a> of 1086 in reference to the county of <a href="/wiki/Dorset" title="Dorset">Dorset</a>, which is today <a href="/wiki/Broadmayne" title="Broadmayne">Broadmayne</a>, just southeast of <a href="/wiki/Dorchester,_Dorset" title="Dorchester, Dorset">Dorchester</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fisher2002_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fisher2002-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>The view generally held among British place name scholars is that Mayne in Dorset is <a href="/wiki/Brittonic_languages" title="Brittonic languages">Brythonic</a>, corresponding to modern <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a> "maen", plural "main" or "meini".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Some early spellings are: MAINE 1086, MEINE 1200, MEINES 1204, MAYNE 1236.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Today the village is known as <a href="/wiki/Broadmayne" title="Broadmayne">Broadmayne</a>, which is primitive Welsh or Brythonic, "main" meaning rock or stone, considered a reference to the many large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sarsen_stone" title="Sarsen stone">sarsen stones</a> still present around Little Mayne farm, half a mile northeast of Broadmayne village.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first known record of the name appears in an August 10, 1622, land charter to Sir Ferdinando Gorges and Captain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Mason_(c.1600-1672)" title="John Mason (c.1600-1672)">John Mason</a>, English <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> veterans, who were granted a large tract in present-day Maine that Mason and Gorges "intend to name the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Maine" title="Province of Maine">Province of Maine</a>". Mason had served with the Royal Navy in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orkney_Islands" title="Orkney Islands">Orkney Islands</a> where the chief island is called <a href="/wiki/Mainland,_Orkney" title="Mainland, Orkney">Mainland</a>, a possible name derivation for these English sailors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stewart_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Stewart-11">[11]</a></sup> In 1623, the English naval captain <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Levett" title="Christopher Levett">Christopher Levett</a>, exploring the New England coast, wrote: "The first place I set my foote upon in New England was the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Shoals" title="Isles of Shoals">Isle of Shoals</a>, being Ilands  [<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>] in the sea, above two Leagues from the Mayne."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Initially, several tracts along the coast of New England were referred to as <i>Main</i> or <i>Maine</i> (cf. the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Main" title="Spanish Main">Spanish Main</a>). A reconfirmed and enhanced April 3, 1639, charter from England's King Charles I gave Sir Ferdinando Gorges increased powers over his new province and stated that it "shall forever hereafter, be called and named the PROVINCE OR COUNTIE OF MAINE, and not by any other name or names whatsoever..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fisher2002_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-Fisher2002-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Maine is the only state whose name has exactly one syllable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Maine" title="History of Maine">History of Maine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumb tright">

<i>Misty Morning, Coast of Maine</i>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
Arthur Parton (1842–1914). Between 1865 and 1870, <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Museum" title="Brooklyn Museum">Brooklyn Museum</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The original inhabitants of the territory that is now Maine were Algonquian-speaking <a href="/wiki/Wabanaki_Confederacy" title="Wabanaki Confederacy">Wabanaki</a> peoples, including the <a href="/wiki/Passamaquoddy" title="Passamaquoddy">Passamaquoddy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maliseet" title="Maliseet">Maliseet</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penobscot_people" title="Penobscot people">Penobscot</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kennebec_tribe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kennebec tribe (page does not exist)">Kennebec</a> and <a href="/wiki/Androscoggin_people" title="Androscoggin people">Androscoggin</a>. During the later King Phillip's War, many of these peoples would merge in one form or another to become the Wabanaki Confederacy, aiding the <a href="/wiki/Wampanoag" title="Wampanoag">Wampanoag</a> of Massachusetts &amp; the <a href="/wiki/Mahican" title="Mahican">Mahican</a> of New York. Afterwards, many of these people were driven from their natural territories, but most of the tribes of Maine continued, unchanged, until the American Revolution. Before this point, however, most of these people were considered separate nations. Many had adapted to living in permanent, Iroquois inspired settlements, while those along the coast tended to be semi-nomadic-- traveling from settlement to settlement on a yearly cycle. They would usually winter inland &amp; head to the coasts by summer. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_exploration_of_North_America" title="European exploration of North America">European</a> contact with what is now called Maine started around 1200 CE when <a href="/wiki/Norse_colonization_of_North_America" title="Norse colonization of North America">Norwegians</a> interacted with the native <a href="/wiki/Penobscot" title="Penobscot">Penobscot</a> in present-day <a href="/wiki/Hancock_County,_Maine" title="Hancock County, Maine">Hancock County</a>, most likely through trade. About 200 years earlier, from the settlements of <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>, Norwegians had <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norse_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Norse colonization of the Americas">discovered America</a> and <a href="/wiki/L%27Anse_aux_Meadows" title="L'Anse aux Meadows">attempted to settle</a> areas such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newfoundland" title="Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a>, but failed to establish a permanent settlement there. Archeological evidence suggests that Norwegians in Greenland returned to North America for several <a href="/wiki/Century" title="Century">centuries</a> after the initial discovery to collect timber and to trade, with the most relevant evidence being the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maine_Penny" title="Maine Penny">Maine Penny</a>, a 10th-century Norwegian coin found at a Native American dig site in 1954.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first European settlement in Maine was in 1604 on <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix_Island,_Maine" title="Saint Croix Island, Maine">Saint Croix Island</a>, led by French explorer <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Dugua,_Sieur_de_Mons" title="Pierre Dugua, Sieur de Mons">Pierre Dugua, Sieur de Mons</a>; his party included <a href="/wiki/Samuel_de_Champlain" title="Samuel de Champlain">Samuel de Champlain</a>, noted as an explorer. The French named the entire area <a href="/wiki/Acadia" title="Acadia">Acadia</a>, including the portion that later became the state of Maine. The first English settlement in Maine was established by the <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Company" title="Plymouth Company">Plymouth Company</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Popham_Colony" title="Popham Colony">Popham Colony</a> in 1607, the same year as the settlement at <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">Jamestown, Virginia</a>. The Popham colonists returned to England after 14 months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>The French established two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit" title="Jesuit">Jesuit</a> missions: one on <a href="/wiki/Penobscot_Bay" title="Penobscot Bay">Penobscot Bay</a> in 1609, and the other on <a href="/wiki/Mount_Desert_Island" title="Mount Desert Island">Mount Desert Island</a> in 1613. The same year, <a href="/wiki/Castine,_Maine" title="Castine, Maine">Castine</a> was established by <a href="/wiki/Claude_de_Saint-%C3%89tienne_de_la_Tour" title="Claude de Saint-Étienne de la Tour">Claude de La Tour</a>. In 1625, <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Saint-%C3%89tienne_de_la_Tour" title="Charles de Saint-Étienne de la Tour">Charles de Saint-Étienne de la Tour</a> erected <a href="/wiki/Fort_Pentagouet" title="Fort Pentagouet">Fort Pentagouet</a> to protect Castine. The coastal areas of western Maine first became the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Maine" title="Province of Maine">Province of Maine</a> in a 1622 land patent. Eastern Maine north of the <a href="/wiki/Kennebec_River" title="Kennebec River">Kennebec River</a> was more sparsely settled and was known in the 17th century as the <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Sagadahock" title="Territory of Sagadahock">Territory of Sagadahock</a>. A second settlement was attempted in 1623 by English explorer and naval Captain <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Levett" title="Christopher Levett">Christopher Levett</a> at a place called <a href="/wiki/York,_Maine" title="York, Maine">York</a>, where he had been granted 6,000 acres (24 km<sup>2</sup>) by King <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I of England</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> It also failed.</p>
<p>Central Maine was formerly inhabited by people of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Androscoggin_tribe" title="Androscoggin tribe">Androscoggin tribe</a> of the Abenaki nation, also known as Arosaguntacook. They were driven out of the area in 1690 during <a href="/wiki/King_William%27s_War" title="King William's War">King William's War</a>. They were relocated at <a href="/wiki/Saint-Fran%C3%A7ois-du-Lac,_Quebec" title="Saint-François-du-Lac, Quebec">St. Francis</a>, Canada, which was destroyed by <a href="/wiki/Rogers%27_Rangers" title="Rogers' Rangers">Rogers' Rangers</a> in 1759, and is now <a href="/wiki/Odanak" title="Odanak">Odanak</a>. The other Abenaki tribes suffered several severe defeats, particularly during <a href="/wiki/Dummer%27s_War" title="Dummer's War">Dummer's War</a>, with the capture of <a href="/wiki/Norridgewock" title="Norridgewock">Norridgewock</a> in 1724 and the defeat of the <a href="/wiki/Pequawket" title="Pequawket">Pequawket</a> in 1725, which greatly reduced their numbers. They finally withdrew to <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, where they were settled at <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9cancour,_Quebec" title="Bécancour, Quebec">Bécancour</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sillery,_Quebec_City" title="Sillery, Quebec City">Sillery</a>, and later at St. Francis, along with other refugee tribes from the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>The province within its current boundaries became part of <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Bay_Colony" title="Massachusetts Bay Colony">Massachusetts Bay Colony</a> in 1652. Maine was much fought over by the French, English and allied natives during the 17th and early 18th centuries, who conducted raids against each other, taking captives for ransom or, in some cases, adoption by Native American tribes. A notable example was the early 1692 Abenaki <a href="/wiki/Raid_on_York_(1692)" title="Raid on York (1692)">raid on York</a>, where about 100 English settlers were killed and another estimated 80 taken hostage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The Abenaki took captives taken during raids of Massachusetts in <a href="/wiki/Queen_Anne%27s_War" title="Queen Anne's War">Queen Anne's War</a> of the early 1700s to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kahnewake" title="Kahnewake">Kahnewake</a>, a Catholic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohawk_nation" title="Mohawk nation">Mohawk</a> village near <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, where some were adopted and others ransomed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the British defeated the French in Acadia in the 1740s, the territory from the <a href="/wiki/Penobscot_River" title="Penobscot River">Penobscot River</a> east fell under the nominal authority of the <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Province of Nova Scotia</a>, and together with present-day New Brunswick formed the Nova Scotia county of <a href="/wiki/Sunbury_County,_Nova_Scotia" title="Sunbury County, Nova Scotia">Sunbury</a>, with its court of general sessions at Campobello. American and British forces contended for Maine's territory during the American Revolution and the War of 1812, with the British occupying eastern Maine in both conflicts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The territory of Maine was confirmed as part of Massachusetts when the United States was formed following the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">Treaty of Paris</a> ending the revolution, although the final border with <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North America</a> was not established until the <a href="/wiki/Webster%E2%80%93Ashburton_Treaty" title="Webster–Ashburton Treaty">Webster–Ashburton Treaty</a> of 1842.</p>
<p>Maine was physically separate from the rest of Massachusetts. Long-standing disagreements over land speculation and settlements led to Maine residents and their allies in Massachusetts proper forcing an 1807 vote in the Massachusetts Assembly on permitting Maine to secede; the vote failed. Secessionist sentiment in Maine was stoked during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a> when Massachusetts pro-British merchants opposed the war and refused to defend Maine from British invaders. In 1819, Massachusetts agreed to permit secession, sanctioned by voters of the rapidly growing region the following year. Formal secession and formation of the state of Maine as the 23rd state occurred on March 15, 1820, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Missouri_Compromise" title="Missouri Compromise">Missouri Compromise</a>, which geographically limited the spread of <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a> and enabled the admission to statehood of <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a> the following year, keeping a balance between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_state" title="Slave state">slave</a> and free states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Maine's original <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capital_(political)" title="Capital (political)">capital</a> was <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Maine" title="Portland, Maine">Portland</a>, Maine's largest city, until it was moved to the more central <a href="/wiki/Augusta,_Maine" title="Augusta, Maine">Augusta</a> in 1832. The principal office of the <a href="/wiki/Maine_Supreme_Judicial_Court" title="Maine Supreme Judicial Court">Maine Supreme Judicial Court</a> remains in Portland.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/20th_Maine_Volunteer_Infantry_Regiment" title="20th Maine Volunteer Infantry Regiment">20th Maine Volunteer Infantry Regiment</a>, under the command of Colonel <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joshua_Lawrence_Chamberlain" title="Joshua Lawrence Chamberlain">Joshua Lawrence Chamberlain</a>, prevented the <a href="/wiki/Union_Army" title="Union Army">Union Army</a> from being flanked at <a href="/wiki/Little_Round_Top" title="Little Round Top">Little Round Top</a> by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Confederate_Army" title="Confederate Army">Confederate Army</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gettysburg" title="Battle of Gettysburg">Battle of Gettysburg</a>.</p>
<p>Four <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">U.S. Navy</a> ships have been named <a href="/wiki/USS_Maine" title="USS Maine">USS <i>Maine</i></a>, most famously the <a href="/wiki/Armored_cruiser" title="Armored cruiser">armored cruiser</a> <a href="/wiki/USS_Maine_(ACR-1)" title="USS Maine (ACR-1)">USS <i>Maine</i> (ACR-1)</a>, whose sinking by an explosion on 15 February 1898 precipitated the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Maine" title="List of counties in Maine">List of counties in Maine</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Maine_rivers" title="List of Maine rivers">List of Maine rivers</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_lakes_in_Maine" title="List of lakes in Maine">List of lakes in Maine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Maine" title="Geology of Maine">Geology of Maine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_New_England" title="Geology of New England">Geology of New England</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:National-atlas-maine.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6312" data-file-width="9313" height="305" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/National-atlas-maine.png/450px-National-atlas-maine.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/National-atlas-maine.png/675px-National-atlas-maine.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/National-atlas-maine.png/900px-National-atlas-maine.png 2x" width="450"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:National-atlas-maine.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A map of Maine and surrounding region</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To the south and east is the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> and to the north and northeast is <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a>, a province of Canada. The Canadian province of <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> is to the northwest. Maine is both the northernmost state in <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> and the largest, accounting for almost half the region's entire land area. Maine is the only state to border only one other state (<a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a> to the west).</p>
<p>Maine is the easternmost state in the United States in both its extreme points and its geographic center. The municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Eastport,_Maine" title="Eastport, Maine">Eastport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lubec,_Maine" title="Lubec, Maine">Lubec</a> are, respectively, the easternmost city and town in the United States. <a href="/wiki/Estcourt_Station,_Maine" title="Estcourt Station, Maine">Estcourt Station</a> is Maine's northernmost point, as well as the northernmost point in New England. (For more information see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extreme_points_of_the_United_States" title="Extreme points of the United States">extreme points of the United States</a>.)</p>
<p>Maine's <a href="/wiki/Moosehead_Lake" title="Moosehead Lake">Moosehead Lake</a> is the largest lake wholly in New England, as <a href="/wiki/Lake_Champlain" title="Lake Champlain">Lake Champlain</a> is located between <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a>, New York and Quebec. A number of other Maine lakes, such as <a href="/wiki/South_Twin_Lake_(Maine)" title="South Twin Lake (Maine)">South Twin Lake</a>, are described by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thoreau" title="Thoreau">Thoreau</a> in <i>The Maine Woods</i> (1864). <a href="/wiki/Mount_Katahdin" title="Mount Katahdin">Mount Katahdin</a> is both the northern terminus of the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Trail" title="Appalachian Trail">Appalachian Trail</a>, which extends southerly to <a href="/wiki/Springer_Mountain" title="Springer Mountain">Springer Mountain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, and the southern terminus of the new <a href="/wiki/International_Appalachian_Trail" title="International Appalachian Trail">International Appalachian Trail</a> which, when complete, will run to <a href="/wiki/Belle_Isle_(Newfoundland_and_Labrador)" title="Belle Isle (Newfoundland and Labrador)">Belle Isle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland and Labrador</a>.</p>
<p>Maine has several unique geographical features. <a href="/wiki/Machias_Seal_Island" title="Machias Seal Island">Machias Seal Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Rock" title="North Rock">North Rock</a>, off its easternmost point, are claimed by both the U.S. and Canada and are within one of <a href="/wiki/List_of_areas_disputed_by_Canada_and_the_United_States" title="List of areas disputed by Canada and the United States">four areas between the two countries whose sovereignty is still in dispute</a>, but it is the only one of the disputed areas containing land. Also in this easternmost area in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Fundy" title="Bay of Fundy">Bay of Fundy</a> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Sow" title="Old Sow">Old Sow</a>, the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tidal" title="Tidal">tidal</a> <a href="/wiki/Whirlpool" title="Whirlpool">whirlpool</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>.</p>
<p>Maine is the least densely populated <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. state</a> east of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a>. It is called the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_nicknames" title="List of U.S. state nicknames">Pine Tree State</a>; about 83% of its land is forested,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forest_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-forest-36">[36]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Forest_cover_by_state_in_the_United_States" title="Forest cover by state in the United States">the most forest cover of any U.S. state</a>. In the forested areas of the interior lies much uninhabited land, some of which does not have formal political organization into local units (a rarity in New England). The <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Aroostook,_Maine" title="Northwest Aroostook, Maine">Northwest Aroostook, Maine</a> <a href="/wiki/Unorganized_territory" title="Unorganized territory">unorganized territory</a> in the northern part of the state, for example, has an area of 2,668 square miles (6,910 km<sup>2</sup>) and a population of 10, or one person for every 267 square miles (690 km<sup>2</sup>).</p>
<p>Maine is in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperate_broadleaf_and_mixed_forests" title="Temperate broadleaf and mixed forests">temperate broadleaf and mixed forests</a> <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">biome</a>. The land near the southern and central Atlantic coast is covered by the mixed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quercus" title="Quercus">oaks</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_coastal_forests" title="Northeastern coastal forests">Northeastern coastal forests</a>. The remainder of the state, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maine_North_Woods" title="Maine North Woods">North Woods</a>, is covered by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_England-Acadian_forests" title="New England-Acadian forests">New England-Acadian forests</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecoregions_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-ecoregions-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Maine has almost 230 miles (400 km) of coastline (and 3,500 miles (5,600 km) of tidal coastline).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mainegovfacts_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-mainegovfacts-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Quoddy_Head" title="West Quoddy Head">West Quoddy Head</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Lubec,_Maine" title="Lubec, Maine">Lubec, Maine</a>, is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extreme_points_of_the_United_States" title="Extreme points of the United States">easternmost point</a> of land in the 48 contiguous states. Along the famous rock-bound coast of Maine are lighthouses, beaches, fishing villages, and thousands of offshore islands, including the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Shoals" title="Isles of Shoals">Isles of Shoals</a> which straddle the New Hampshire border. There are jagged rocks and cliffs and many bays and inlets. Inland are lakes, rivers, forests, and mountains. This visual contrast of forested slopes sweeping down to the sea has been summed up by American poet <a href="/wiki/Edna_St._Vincent_Millay" title="Edna St. Vincent Millay">Edna St. Vincent Millay</a> of <a href="/wiki/Rockland,_Maine" title="Rockland, Maine">Rockland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Camden,_Maine" title="Camden, Maine">Camden</a>, Maine, in "Renascence":</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_beach_in_maine_on_a_clear_day.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1943" data-file-width="2688" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/A_beach_in_maine_on_a_clear_day.jpg/250px-A_beach_in_maine_on_a_clear_day.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/A_beach_in_maine_on_a_clear_day.jpg/375px-A_beach_in_maine_on_a_clear_day.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/A_beach_in_maine_on_a_clear_day.jpg/500px-A_beach_in_maine_on_a_clear_day.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_beach_in_maine_on_a_clear_day.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The coast of Maine near <a href="/wiki/Acadia_National_Park" title="Acadia National Park">Acadia National Park</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Boothbay_Harbor,_summer_morning_at_low_tide.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="333" data-file-width="500" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Boothbay_Harbor%2C_summer_morning_at_low_tide.jpg/250px-Boothbay_Harbor%2C_summer_morning_at_low_tide.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Boothbay_Harbor%2C_summer_morning_at_low_tide.jpg/375px-Boothbay_Harbor%2C_summer_morning_at_low_tide.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0f/Boothbay_Harbor%2C_summer_morning_at_low_tide.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Boothbay_Harbor,_summer_morning_at_low_tide.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Boothbay_Harbor,_Maine" title="Boothbay Harbor, Maine">Boothbay Harbor</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<dl>
<dd>"All I could see from where I stood</dd>
<dd>Was three long mountains and a wood;</dd>
<dd>I turned and looked the other way,</dd>
<dd>And saw three islands in a bay."</dd>
</dl>
<p>Geologists describe this type of landscape as a "drowned coast", where a rising sea level has invaded former land features, creating bays out of valleys and islands out of mountain tops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> A rise in the elevation of the land due to the melting of heavy glacier ice caused a slight rebounding effect of underlying rock; this land rise, however, was not enough to eliminate all the effect of the rising sea level and its invasion of former land features.</p>
<p>Much of Maine's geomorphology was created by extended glacial activity at the end of the <a href="/wiki/Quaternary_glaciation" title="Quaternary glaciation">last ice age</a>. Prominent glacial features include <a href="/wiki/Somes_Sound" title="Somes Sound">Somes Sound</a> and Bubble Rock, both part of Acadia National Park on Mount Desert Island. Carved by glaciers, Somes Sound is considered to be the only <a href="/wiki/Fjord" title="Fjord">fjord</a> on the eastern seaboard and reaches depths of 175 feet (50 m). The extreme depth and steep drop-off allow large ships to navigate almost the entire length of the sound. These features also have made it attractive for boat builders, such as the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Hinckley_Yachts" title="Hinckley Yachts">Hinckley Yachts</a>.</p>
<p>Bubble Rock, a <a href="/wiki/Glacial_erratic" title="Glacial erratic">glacial erratic</a>, is a large boulder perched on the edge of Bubble Mountain in <a href="/wiki/Acadia_National_Park" title="Acadia National Park">Acadia National Park</a>. By analyzing the type of granite, geologists were able to discover that glaciers carried Bubble Rock to its present location from near the town of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lucerne,_Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lucerne, Maine (page does not exist)">Lucerne, Maine</a> – 30 miles (48 km) away. The <a href="/wiki/Iapetus_Suture" title="Iapetus Suture">Iapetus Suture</a> runs through the north and west of the state, being underlain by the ancient <a href="/wiki/Laurentia" title="Laurentia">Laurentian terrane</a>, and the south and east underlain by the <a href="/wiki/Avalonia" title="Avalonia">Avalonian terrane</a>.</p>
<p>Acadia National Park is the only national park in New England. Areas under the protection and management of the <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a> include:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Acadia National Park near <a href="/wiki/Bar_Harbor,_Maine" title="Bar Harbor, Maine">Bar Harbor</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Trail" title="Appalachian Trail">Appalachian National Scenic Trail</a></li>
<li>Maine Acadian Culture in St. John Valley</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Campobello_International_Park" title="Roosevelt Campobello International Park">Roosevelt Campobello International Park</a> on <a href="/wiki/Campobello_Island" title="Campobello Island">Campobello Island</a>, New Brunswick, Canada, operated by both the US and Canada, just across the <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt_Bridge" title="Franklin Delano Roosevelt Bridge">Franklin Delano Roosevelt Bridge</a> from <a href="/wiki/Lubec,_Maine" title="Lubec, Maine">Lubec</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Croix_Island_International_Historic_Site" title="Saint Croix Island International Historic Site">Saint Croix Island International Historic Site</a> at <a href="/wiki/Calais,_Maine" title="Calais, Maine">Calais</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Katahdin_Woods_and_Waters_National_Monument" title="Katahdin Woods and Waters National Monument">Katahdin Woods and Waters National Monument</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Maine_state_parks" title="List of Maine state parks">Maine State Parks</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maine_Wildlife_Management_Areas_(WMA)" title="Maine Wildlife Management Areas (WMA)">Maine Wildlife Management Areas (WMA)</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stratton_Flagstaff_Lake_Maine_262258633.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2404" data-file-width="3208" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Stratton_Flagstaff_Lake_Maine_262258633.jpg/220px-Stratton_Flagstaff_Lake_Maine_262258633.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Stratton_Flagstaff_Lake_Maine_262258633.jpg/330px-Stratton_Flagstaff_Lake_Maine_262258633.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Stratton_Flagstaff_Lake_Maine_262258633.jpg/440px-Stratton_Flagstaff_Lake_Maine_262258633.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stratton_Flagstaff_Lake_Maine_262258633.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Autumn in Stratton</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bangor_Maine.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Bangor_Maine.JPG/220px-Bangor_Maine.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Bangor_Maine.JPG/330px-Bangor_Maine.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Bangor_Maine.JPG/440px-Bangor_Maine.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bangor_Maine.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Winter in <a href="/wiki/Bangor,_Maine" title="Bangor, Maine">Bangor</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Maine has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i>Dfb</i>), with warm (although generally not hot), humid summers. Winters are cold and snowy throughout the state, and are especially severe in the northern parts of Maine. Coastal areas are moderated somewhat by the Atlantic Ocean, resulting in milder winters and cooler summers in immediate coastal areas. Daytime highs are generally in the 75–80 °F (24–27 °C) range throughout the state in July, with overnight lows in the high 50s °F (around 15 °C). January temperatures range from highs near 32 °F (0 °C) on the southern coast to overnight lows averaging below 0 °F (−18 °C) in the far north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usgs_a_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-usgs_a-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state's record high temperature is 105 °F (41 °C), set in July 1911, at North Bridgton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday-43">[43]</a></sup> Precipitation in Maine is evenly distributed year-round, but with a slight summer maximum in northern/northwestern Maine and a slight late-fall or early-winter maximum along the coast due to "nor'easters" or intense cold-season storms. In coastal Maine, the late spring and summer months are usually driest – a rarity across the Eastern United States. Maine has fewer days of thunderstorms than any other state east of the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rockies</a>, with most of the state averaging less than 20 days of <a href="/wiki/Thunderstorm" title="Thunderstorm">thunderstorms</a> a year. <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">Tornadoes</a> are rare in Maine, with the state averaging fewer than two per year, mostly occurring in the southern part of the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Annual_average_number_of_tornadoes_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Annual_average_number_of_tornadoes-44">[44]</a></sup> Maine rarely sees <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclones</a>.</p>
<p>In January 2009, a new record low temperature for the state was set at <a href="/wiki/Big_Black_River_(Saint_John_River)" title="Big Black River (Saint John River)">Big Black River</a> of −50 °F (−46 °C), tying the New England record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usgs_a_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-usgs_a-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>Annual precipitation varies from 909 mm (35.8 in) in <a href="/wiki/Presque_Isle,_Maine" title="Presque Isle, Maine">Presque Isle</a>, to 1,441 mm (56.7 in) in Acadia National Park.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>

<p><br/>
The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimates that the population of Maine was 1,329,328 on July 1, 2015, a 0.07% increase since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-48">[48]</a></sup> The population density of the state is 41.3 people per square mile, making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_population_density" title="List of U.S. states by population density">least densely populated state</a> in New England, the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">American northeast</a>, the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">eastern seaboard</a>, of all of the states with an Atlantic coastline and of all of the states east of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a>.</p>
<p>The mean population center of Maine is located in <a href="/wiki/Kennebec_County,_Maine" title="Kennebec County, Maine">Kennebec County</a>, just east of <a href="/wiki/Augusta,_Maine" title="Augusta, Maine">Augusta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mean_population_center_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-mean_population_center-49">[49]</a></sup> The Greater Portland metropolitan area is the most densely populated with nearly 40% of Maine's population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metropolitan_populations.2C_census.gov_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Metropolitan_populations.2C_census.gov-50">[50]</a></sup> As explained in detail under "Geography", there are large tracts of uninhabited land in some remote parts of the interior.</p>
<h3><span id="Race,_ancestry_and_language"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Race.2C_ancestry_and_language">Race, ancestry and language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Race, ancestry and language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At the 2010 Census, 94.4% of the population was non-Hispanic White, 1.1% non-Hispanic Black or African American, 0.6% American Indian and Alaska Native, 1.0% Asian, 0.1% from some other race and 1.4% of two or more races. 1.3% of Maine's population was of Hispanic, Latino, or Spanish origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maine_population_map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="325" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Maine_population_map.png/325px-Maine_population_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Maine_population_map.png/488px-Maine_population_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3d/Maine_population_map.png 2x" width="325"/></a>

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maine_population_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maine population density map</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>People citing that they are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_ethnicity" title="American ethnicity">American</a> are of overwhelmingly English descent, but have ancestry that has been in the region for so long (often since the 1600s) that they choose to identify simply as Americans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>Maine has the highest percentage of <a href="/wiki/French_Americans" title="French Americans">French Americans</a> among American states. It also has the highest percentage of non-Hispanic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">whites</a> of any state, at 94.4% of the total population, according to the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 Census</a>. In 2011, 89.0% of all births in the state were to non-Hispanic white parents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The state also has the highest percentage of French-speakers of any state. Most of the French in Maine are of Canadian Origin, but in some cases have been living there prior to the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>. There are particularly high concentrations of French in the northern part of Maine in <a href="/wiki/Aroostook_County,_Maine" title="Aroostook County, Maine">Aroostook County</a>, which is part of a cultural region known as <a href="/wiki/Acadia" title="Acadia">Acadia</a> that goes over the border into <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a>. Along with the <a href="/wiki/Acadians" title="Acadians">Acadian</a> population in the north, many French came from <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> as immigrants between 1840 and 1930. Census figures show that Maine has the highest percentage of people speaking French at home of any state: 5.28% of Maine households are French-speaking, compared with 4.68% in <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, which is the second highest state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> French-speakers are the state's chief linguistic minority; the 2000 Census reported 92.25% of Maine residents aged five and older spoke only English at home. Maine does not have an official language,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-language_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-language-2">[2]</a></sup> but the most widely spoken language in the state is English. Spanish is the third-most-spoken language in Maine, after English and French.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>The upper <a href="/wiki/Saint_John_River_(Bay_of_Fundy)" title="Saint John River (Bay of Fundy)">Saint John River</a> valley area was once part of the so-called <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Madawaska" title="Republic of Madawaska">Republic of Madawaska</a>, before the frontier was decided in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Webster-Ashburton_Treaty" title="Webster-Ashburton Treaty">Webster-Ashburton Treaty</a> of 1842. Over one quarter of the population of <a href="/wiki/Lewiston,_Maine" title="Lewiston, Maine">Lewiston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waterville,_Maine" title="Waterville, Maine">Waterville</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biddeford" title="Biddeford">Biddeford</a> are Franco-American. Most of the residents of the <a href="/wiki/Mid_Coast" title="Mid Coast">Mid Coast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Down_East" title="Down East">Down East</a> sections are chiefly of British heritage. Smaller numbers of various other groups, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">Irish</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">Italian</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_American" title="Polish American">Polish</a>, have settled throughout the state since the late 19th and early 20th century <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigration</a> waves.</p>
