<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Religion_Data_Archives" title="Association of Religion Data Archives">Association of Religion Data Archives</a> (ARDA),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.thearda.com_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.thearda.com-69">[69]</a></sup> the religious affiliations of Maine in 2010 were:</p>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">Catholic Church</a> – 28%</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> – 7%</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangelical_Protestant" title="Evangelical Protestant">Evangelical Protestant</a> – 4%</li>
<li>Other religions – 1.7%</li>
<li>Non-Christian religions include <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD" title="Bahá'í">Bahá'í</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>The Catholic Church was the largest religious institution with 202,106 members, the <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">United Methodist Church</a> had 28,329 members, the <a href="/wiki/United_Church_of_Christ" title="United Church of Christ">United Church of Christ</a> had 22,747 members</p>
<p>In 2010, a study named Maine as the least religious state in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hendrickson_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hendrickson-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maine_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="Maine locations by per capita income">Maine locations by per capita income</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TotallyFreeImages_com-280902-Standard-preview.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="230" data-file-width="450" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/TotallyFreeImages_com-280902-Standard-preview.jpg/250px-TotallyFreeImages_com-280902-Standard-preview.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/TotallyFreeImages_com-280902-Standard-preview.jpg/375px-TotallyFreeImages_com-280902-Standard-preview.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bd/TotallyFreeImages_com-280902-Standard-preview.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TotallyFreeImages_com-280902-Standard-preview.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stereoscopic" title="Stereoscopic">Stereoscopic</a> view "Lobster pots ready for placing" ~ 1928</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Biw_aerial.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="367" data-file-width="550" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Biw_aerial.jpg/250px-Biw_aerial.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Biw_aerial.jpg/375px-Biw_aerial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Biw_aerial.jpg/500px-Biw_aerial.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Biw_aerial.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bath_Iron_Works" title="Bath Iron Works">Bath Iron Works</a> naval shipbuilding</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Economic_Analysis" title="Bureau of Economic Analysis">Bureau of Economic Analysis</a> estimates that Maine's total gross state product for 2010 was $52 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_personal_income_in_the_United_States" title="Per capita personal income in the United States">per capita personal income</a> for 2007 was US$33,991, 34th in the nation. As of April 2016, Maine's unemployment rate is 3.4%<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Old_Port_area_of_Portland,_ME.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2379" data-file-width="3189" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Old_Port_area_of_Portland%2C_ME.jpg/250px-Old_Port_area_of_Portland%2C_ME.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Old_Port_area_of_Portland%2C_ME.jpg/375px-Old_Port_area_of_Portland%2C_ME.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Old_Port_area_of_Portland%2C_ME.jpg/500px-Old_Port_area_of_Portland%2C_ME.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Old_Port_area_of_Portland,_ME.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Old port area of <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Maine" title="Portland, Maine">Portland</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Maine's <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agricultural</a> outputs include poultry, eggs, dairy products, cattle, wild blueberries, apples, <a href="/wiki/Maple_syrup" title="Maple syrup">maple syrup</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maple_sugar" title="Maple sugar">maple sugar</a>. <a href="/wiki/Aroostook_County,_Maine" title="Aroostook County, Maine">Aroostook County</a> is known for its <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potato</a> crops. <a href="/wiki/Commercial_fishing" title="Commercial fishing">Commercial fishing</a>, once a mainstay of the state's economy, maintains a presence, particularly <a href="/wiki/Lobster_fishing" title="Lobster fishing">lobstering</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Groundfishing" title="Groundfishing">groundfishing</a>. Western Maine aquifers and springs are a major source of bottled water.</p>
<p>Maine's industrial outputs consist chiefly of paper, lumber and wood products, electronic equipment, leather products, food products, textiles, and bio-technology. Naval shipbuilding and construction remain key as well, with <a href="/wiki/Bath_Iron_Works" title="Bath Iron Works">Bath Iron Works</a> in Bath and <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Naval_Shipyard" title="Portsmouth Naval Shipyard">Portsmouth Naval Shipyard</a> in Kittery.</p>
<p>Brunswick Landing, formerly <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Brunswick" title="Naval Air Station Brunswick">Naval Air Station Brunswick</a>, is also in Maine. Formerly a large support base for the U.S. Navy, the <a href="/wiki/Base_Realignment_and_Closure" title="Base Realignment and Closure">BRAC</a> campaign initiated the Naval Air Station's closing, despite a government-funded effort to upgrade its facilities. The former base has since been changed into a civilian business park, as well as a new satellite campus for <a href="/wiki/Southern_Maine_Community_College" title="Southern Maine Community College">Southern Maine Community College</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Maine is the number one US producer of low-bush <a href="/wiki/Blueberry" title="Blueberry">blueberries</a> (<a href="/wiki/Vaccinium_angustifolium" title="Vaccinium angustifolium">Vaccinium angustifolium</a>). Preliminary data from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USDA" title="USDA">USDA</a> for 2012 also indicate Maine was the largest blueberry producer of the major blueberry producing states in the US, with 91,100,000 lbs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> This data includes both low (wild), and high-bush (cultivated) blueberries: <a href="/wiki/Vaccinium_corymbosum" title="Vaccinium corymbosum">Vaccinium corymbosum</a>. The largest toothpick manufacturing plant in the United States used to be located in <a href="/wiki/Strong,_Maine" title="Strong, Maine">Strong, Maine</a>. The Strong Wood Products plant produced 20 million toothpicks a day. It closed in May 2003.</p>
<p>Tourism and outdoor recreation play a major and increasingly important role in Maine's economy. The state is a popular destination for sport <a href="/wiki/Hunting" title="Hunting">hunting</a> (particularly deer, moose and bear), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sport_fishing" title="Sport fishing">sport fishing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snowmobile" title="Snowmobile">snowmobiling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skiing</a>, boating, <a href="/wiki/Camping" title="Camping">camping</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hiking" title="Hiking">hiking</a>, among other activities.</p>
<p>Historically, Maine ports played a key role in national transportation. Beginning around 1880, Portland's rail link and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ice-free_port" title="Ice-free port">ice-free port</a> made it Canada's principal winter port, until the aggressive development of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Halifax_Regional_Municipality,_Nova_Scotia" title="Halifax Regional Municipality, Nova Scotia">Halifax</a>, Nova Scotia, in the mid-1900s. In 2013, 12,039,600 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Short_tons" title="Short tons">short tons</a> passed into and out of Portland by sea,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> which places it 45th of US water ports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Portland Maine's <a href="/wiki/Portland_International_Jetport" title="Portland International Jetport">Portland International Jetport</a> was recently expanded, providing the state with increased air traffic from carriers such as <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Airlines" title="Southwest Airlines">Southwest Airlines</a>.</p>
<p>Maine has very few large companies that maintain headquarters in the state, and that number has fallen due to consolidations and mergers, particularly in the <a href="/wiki/Pulp_and_paper_industry" title="Pulp and paper industry">pulp and paper industry</a>. Some of the larger companies that do maintain headquarters in Maine include <a href="/wiki/Fairchild_Semiconductor" title="Fairchild Semiconductor">Fairchild Semiconductor</a> in South Portland; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IDEXX_Laboratories" title="IDEXX Laboratories">IDEXX Laboratories</a>, in Westbrook; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hannaford_Bros._Co." title="Hannaford Bros. Co.">Hannaford Bros. Co.</a> in Scarborough, <a href="/wiki/Unum" title="Unum">Unum</a> in Portland; <a href="/wiki/TD_Banknorth" title="TD Banknorth">TD Bank</a>, in Portland; <a href="/wiki/L.L.Bean" title="L.L.Bean">L.L.Bean</a> in Freeport; and <a href="/wiki/Cole_Haan" title="Cole Haan">Cole Haan</a> in Yarmouth. Maine is also the home of <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Laboratory" title="Jackson Laboratory">The Jackson Laboratory</a>, the world's largest non-profit mammalian genetic research facility and the world's largest supplier of genetically purebred mice.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxation">Taxation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Taxation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Maine has an <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a> structure containing two brackets, 6.5% to 7.95% of personal income.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Before July 2013 Maine had four brackets: 2%, 4.5%, 7%, and 8.5%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Maine's general <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">sales tax</a> rate is 5.5%. The state also levies charges of 7% on lodging and prepared food and 10% on short-term auto rentals. Commercial sellers of blueberries, a Maine staple, must keep records of their transactions and pay the state 1.5 cents per pound ($1.50 per 100 pounds) of the fruit sold each season. All <a href="/wiki/Real_property" title="Real property">real</a> and tangible <a href="/wiki/Personal_property" title="Personal property">personal property</a> located in the state of Maine is taxable unless specifically exempted by statute. The administration of property taxes is handled by the local assessor in incorporated cities and towns, while property taxes in the unorganized territories are handled by the State Tax Assessor.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shipbuilding">Shipbuilding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Shipbuilding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Bath_Iron_Works" title="Bath Iron Works">Bath Iron Works</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Naval_Shipyard" title="Portsmouth Naval Shipyard">Portsmouth Naval Shipyard</a></div>
<p>Maine has a longstanding tradition of being home to many shipbuilding companies. In the 18th and 19th centuries, Maine was home to many shipyards that produced wooden sailing ships. The main function of these ships was to transport either cargos or passengers overseas. One of these yards was located in <a href="/wiki/Pennellville_Historic_District" title="Pennellville Historic District">Pennellville Historic District</a> in what is now Brunswick, Maine. This yard, owned by the Pennell family, was typical of the many family-owned shipbuilding companies of the time period. Other such examples of shipbuilding families were the Skolfields and the Morses. During the 18th and 19th centuries, wooden shipbuilding of this sort made up a sizable portion of the economy.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KPWM_Aerial_Wiki.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="594" data-file-width="830" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/KPWM_Aerial_Wiki.jpg/250px-KPWM_Aerial_Wiki.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/KPWM_Aerial_Wiki.jpg/375px-KPWM_Aerial_Wiki.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/KPWM_Aerial_Wiki.jpg/500px-KPWM_Aerial_Wiki.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KPWM_Aerial_Wiki.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Portland_International_Jetport" title="Portland International Jetport">Portland International Jetport</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Maine receives <a href="/wiki/Jet_airliner" title="Jet airliner">passenger jet</a> service at its two largest airports, the <a href="/wiki/Portland_International_Jetport" title="Portland International Jetport">Portland International Jetport</a> in Portland, and the <a href="/wiki/Bangor_International_Airport" title="Bangor International Airport">Bangor International Airport</a> in Bangor. Both are served daily by many major <a href="/wiki/Airline" title="Airline">airlines</a> to destinations such as New York, <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando</a>. <a href="/wiki/Essential_Air_Service" title="Essential Air Service">Essential Air Service</a> also subsidizes service to a number of smaller airports in Maine, bringing small <a href="/wiki/Turboprop" title="Turboprop">turboprop</a> aircraft to regional airports such as the <a href="/wiki/Augusta_State_Airport" title="Augusta State Airport">Augusta State Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hancock_County-Bar_Harbor_Airport" title="Hancock County-Bar Harbor Airport">Hancock County-Bar Harbor Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Knox_County_Regional_Airport" title="Knox County Regional Airport">Knox County Regional Airport</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Maine_Regional_Airport_at_Presque_Isle" title="Northern Maine Regional Airport at Presque Isle">Northern Maine Regional Airport at Presque Isle</a>. These airports are served by Cape Air with Cessna 402s and Penair with Saab 340s.</p>
<p>Many smaller airports are scattered throughout Maine, only serving <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a> traffic. The <a href="/wiki/Eastport_Municipal_Airport" title="Eastport Municipal Airport">Eastport Municipal Airport</a>, for example, is a city-owned public-use airport with 1,200 general aviation aircraft operations each year from single-engine and ultralight aircraft.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Highways">Highways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Highways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PenobscotNarrowsBridgeBucksport.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1156" data-file-width="1552" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/PenobscotNarrowsBridgeBucksport.jpg/220px-PenobscotNarrowsBridgeBucksport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/PenobscotNarrowsBridgeBucksport.jpg/330px-PenobscotNarrowsBridgeBucksport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/PenobscotNarrowsBridgeBucksport.jpg/440px-PenobscotNarrowsBridgeBucksport.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PenobscotNarrowsBridgeBucksport.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penobscot_Narrows_Bridge" title="Penobscot Narrows Bridge">Penobscot Narrows Bridge</a>, carrying <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1" title="U.S. Route 1">U.S. Route 1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maine_State_Route_3" title="Maine State Route 3">Maine State Route 3</a> over the <a href="/wiki/Penobscot_River" title="Penobscot River">Penobscot River</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Maine" title="Interstate 95 in Maine">Interstate 95</a> (I-95) travels through Maine, as well as its easterly branch <a href="/wiki/Interstate_295_(Maine)" title="Interstate 295 (Maine)">I-295</a> and spurs <a href="/wiki/Interstate_195_(Maine)" title="Interstate 195 (Maine)">195</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interstate_395_(Maine)" title="Interstate 395 (Maine)">395</a> and the unsigned <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_495_(Maine)" title="Interstate 495 (Maine)">I-495</a>. In addition, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1_in_Maine" title="U.S. Route 1 in Maine">U.S. Route 1</a> (US 1) starts in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Kent,_Maine" title="Fort Kent, Maine">Fort Kent</a> and travels to <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>. The eastern terminus of the eastern section of <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_2_in_Maine" title="U.S. Route 2 in Maine">US 2</a> starts in Houlton, near the New Brunswick, Canada border to <a href="/wiki/Rouses_Point,_New_York" title="Rouses Point, New York">Rouses Point</a>, New York, at <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_11_in_New_York" title="U.S. Route 11 in New York">US 11</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Route_2A_(Maine)" title="U.S. Route 2A (Maine)">US 2A</a> connects Old Town and Orono, primarily serving the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maine" title="University of Maine">University of Maine</a> campus. <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_201" title="U.S. Route 201">US 201</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Route_202_in_Maine" title="U.S. Route 202 in Maine">US 202</a> flow through the state. US 2, <a href="/wiki/Maine_State_Route_6" title="Maine State Route 6">Maine State Route 6</a> (Route 6), and <a href="/wiki/Maine_State_Route_9" title="Maine State Route 9">Route 9</a> are often used by truckers and other motorists of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maritime_Provinces" title="Maritime Provinces">Maritime Provinces</a> <i>en route</i> to other destinations in the United States or as a short cut to <a href="/wiki/Central_Canada" title="Central Canada">Central Canada</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Maine_railroads" title="List of Maine railroads">List of Maine railroads</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger">Passenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Passenger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amtrak_downeaster_ocean_park_2005.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="693" data-file-width="498" height="306" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Amtrak_downeaster_ocean_park_2005.jpg/220px-Amtrak_downeaster_ocean_park_2005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Amtrak_downeaster_ocean_park_2005.jpg/330px-Amtrak_downeaster_ocean_park_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Amtrak_downeaster_ocean_park_2005.jpg/440px-Amtrak_downeaster_ocean_park_2005.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Amtrak_downeaster_ocean_park_2005.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A southbound <i><a href="/wiki/Downeaster_(train)" title="Downeaster (train)">Downeaster</a></i> passenger train at <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Park,_Maine" title="Ocean Park, Maine">Ocean Park, Maine</a>, as viewed from the cab of a northbound train</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Downeaster_(train)" title="Downeaster (train)">Downeaster</a></i> passenger train, operated by <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a>, provides passenger service between Brunswick and Boston's <a href="/wiki/North_Station" title="North Station">North Station</a>, with stops in Freeport, Portland, Old Orchard Beach, Saco, and Wells. The <i>Downeaster</i> makes five daily trips, two of which continue past Portland to <a href="/wiki/Brunswick,_Maine" title="Brunswick, Maine">Brunswick</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Freight">Freight</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Freight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Freight service throughout the state is provided by a handful of regional and shortline carriers: <a href="/wiki/Pan_Am_Railways" title="Pan Am Railways">Pan Am Railways</a> (formerly known as Guilford Rail System), which operates the former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boston_and_Maine_Railroad" title="Boston and Maine Railroad">Boston &amp; Maine</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maine_Central_Railroad" title="Maine Central Railroad">Maine Central</a> railroads; <a href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_and_Atlantic_Railroad" title="St. Lawrence and Atlantic Railroad">St. Lawrence and Atlantic Railroad</a>; <a href="/wiki/Maine_Eastern_Railroad" title="Maine Eastern Railroad">Maine Eastern Railroad</a>; <a href="/wiki/Central_Maine_and_Quebec_Railway" title="Central Maine and Quebec Railway">Central Maine and Quebec Railway</a>; and <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick_Southern_Railway" title="New Brunswick Southern Railway">New Brunswick Southern Railway</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_government">Law and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Law and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Maine" title="List of Governors of Maine">List of Governors of Maine</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Senators_from_Maine" title="List of United States Senators from Maine">List of United States Senators from Maine</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Maine_State_Senators" title="List of Maine State Senators">List of Maine State Senators</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Electoral_reform_in_Maine" title="Electoral reform in Maine">Electoral reform in Maine</a></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maine_Constitution" title="Maine Constitution">Maine Constitution</a> structures Maine's state government, composed of three co-equal branches—the executive, legislative, and judicial branches. The state of Maine also has three Constitutional Officers (the Secretary of State, the State Treasurer, and the State Attorney General) and one Statutory Officer (the State Auditor).</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_branch" title="Legislative branch">legislative branch</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Maine_Legislature" title="Maine Legislature">Maine Legislature</a>, a bicameral body composed of the <a href="/wiki/Maine_House_of_Representatives" title="Maine House of Representatives">Maine House of Representatives</a>, with 151 members, and the <a href="/wiki/Maine_Senate" title="Maine Senate">Maine Senate</a>, with 35 members. The Legislature is charged with introducing and passing laws.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_branch" title="Executive branch">executive branch</a> is responsible for the execution of the laws created by the Legislature and is headed by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Maine" title="Governor of Maine">Governor of Maine</a> (currently Paul LePage). The Governor is elected every four years; no individual may serve more than two consecutive terms in this office. The current <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Attorney_general_of_Maine" title="Attorney general of Maine">attorney general of Maine</a> is <a href="/wiki/Janet_T._Mills" title="Janet T. Mills">Janet T. Mills</a>. As with other <a href="/wiki/State_legislature_(United_States)" title="State legislature (United States)">state legislatures</a>, the Maine Legislature can by a two-thirds majority vote from both the House and Senate override a gubernatorial veto. Maine is one of seven states that do not have a lieutenant governor.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judicial_branch" title="Judicial branch">judicial branch</a> is responsible for interpreting state laws. The highest court of the state is the <a href="/wiki/Maine_Supreme_Judicial_Court" title="Maine Supreme Judicial Court">Maine Supreme Judicial Court</a>. The lower courts are the District Court, <a href="/wiki/Maine_Superior_Court" title="Maine Superior Court">Superior Court</a> and Probate Court. All judges except for probate judges serve full-time, are nominated by the Governor and confirmed by the Legislature for terms of seven years. Probate judges serve part-time and are elected by the voters of each county for four-year terms.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Counties">Counties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Counties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Maine" title="List of counties in Maine">List of counties in Maine</a></div>
<p>Maine is divided into political jurisdictions designated as <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">counties</a>. Since 1860 there have been 16 counties in the state, ranging in size from 370 to 6,829 square miles (958 to 17,700 km<sup>2</sup>).</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_and_local_politics">State and local politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: State and local politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>In state <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_elections" title="General elections">general elections</a>, Maine voters tend to accept <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independent_(politician)" title="Independent (politician)">independent</a> and third-party candidates more frequently than most states. Maine has had two independent governors recently (<a href="/wiki/James_B._Longley" title="James B. Longley">James B. Longley</a>, 1975–1979 and <a href="/wiki/Angus_King" title="Angus King">Angus King</a>, 1995–2003). Maine state politicians, Democrats and Republicans alike, are noted for having more moderate views than many in the national wings of their respective parties.</p>
<p>Maine is an <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage_control_state" title="Alcoholic beverage control state">alcoholic beverage control state</a>.</p>
<p>On May 6, 2009, Maine became the fifth state to legalize <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Maine" title="Same-sex marriage in Maine">same-sex marriage</a>; however, the law was repealed by voters on November 3, 2009. On November 6, 2012, Maine, along with Maryland and Washington, became the first state to legalize same-sex marriage at the ballot box.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_politics">Federal politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Federal politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:United_States_presidential_election_in_Maine,_2016.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3201" data-file-width="2904" height="265" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/United_States_presidential_election_in_Maine%2C_2016.svg/240px-United_States_presidential_election_in_Maine%2C_2016.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/United_States_presidential_election_in_Maine%2C_2016.svg/360px-United_States_presidential_election_in_Maine%2C_2016.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/United_States_presidential_election_in_Maine%2C_2016.svg/480px-United_States_presidential_election_in_Maine%2C_2016.svg.png 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:United_States_presidential_election_in_Maine,_2016.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treemap" title="Treemap">Treemap</a> of the popular vote by county, 2016 presidential election</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 1930s, Maine was one of very few states which retained <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> sentiments. In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1936" title="United States presidential election, 1936">1936 presidential election</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> received the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" title="Electoral College (United States)">electoral votes</a> of every state other than Maine and <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a>; these were the only two states in the nation that never voted for Roosevelt in any of his presidential campaigns, though Maine was closely fought in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1940" title="United States presidential election, 1940">1940</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1944" title="United States presidential election, 1944">1944</a>. In the 1960s, Maine began to lean toward the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrats</a>, especially in <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">presidential</a> elections. In <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1968" title="United States presidential election, 1968">1968</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Humphrey" title="Hubert Humphrey">Hubert Humphrey</a> became just the second Democrat in half a century to carry Maine, perhaps because of the presence of his running mate, Maine Senator <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Muskie" title="Edmund Muskie">Edmund Muskie</a>, although the state voted Republican in every presidential election in the 1970s and 1980s.</p>
<p>Since 1969, two of Maine's four electoral votes have been awarded based on the winner of the statewide election; the other two go to the highest vote-getter in each of the state's two congressional districts. Every other state except <a href="/wiki/Nebraska" title="Nebraska">Nebraska</a> gives all its electoral votes to the candidate who wins the popular vote in the state at large, without regard to performance within districts. Maine split its electoral vote for the first time in 2016, with Donald Trump's strong showing in central and northern Maine allowing him to capture one of the state's four votes in the Electoral College.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ross_Perot" title="Ross Perot">Ross Perot</a> achieved a great deal of success in Maine in the presidential elections of <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1992" title="United States presidential election, 1992">1992</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1996" title="United States presidential election, 1996">1996</a>. In 1992, as an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independent_(politician)" title="Independent (politician)">independent candidate</a>, Perot came in second to Democrat <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, despite the longtime presence of the <a href="/wiki/Bush_family" title="Bush family">Bush family</a> summer home in <a href="/wiki/Kennebunkport,_Maine" title="Kennebunkport, Maine">Kennebunkport</a>. In 1996, as the nominee of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reform_Party_(United_States)" title="Reform Party (United States)">Reform Party</a>, Perot did better in Maine than in any other state.</p>
<p>Maine has voted for Democratic <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> twice, <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a> in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2000" title="United States presidential election, 2000">2000</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2004" title="United States presidential election, 2004">2004</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2008" title="United States presidential election, 2008">2008</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2012" title="United States presidential election, 2012">2012</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2016" title="United States presidential election, 2016">2016 election</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Donald_J._Trump" title="Donald J. Trump">Donald J. Trump</a> won one of Maine's electoral votes with Hillary Clinton winning the other three. Although Democrats have mostly carried the state in presidential elections in recent years, Republicans have largely maintained their control of the state's <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">U.S. Senate</a> seats, with Edmund Muskie, <a href="/wiki/William_Hathaway" title="William Hathaway">William Hathaway</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_J._Mitchell" title="George J. Mitchell">George J. Mitchell</a> being the only Maine Democrats serving in the U.S. Senate in the past fifty years.</p>
<p>In the 2010 midterm elections, Republicans made major gains in Maine. They captured the governor's office as well as majorities in both chambers of the state legislature for the first time since the early 1970s. However, in 2012 elections Democrats managed to recapture both houses of <a href="/wiki/Maine_Legislature" title="Maine Legislature">Maine Legislature</a>.</p>
<p>Maine's U.S. senators are Republican <a href="/wiki/Susan_Collins" title="Susan Collins">Susan Collins</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independent_(politics)" title="Independent (politics)">Independent</a> <a href="/wiki/Angus_King" title="Angus King">Angus King</a>. The governor is Republican <a href="/wiki/Paul_LePage" title="Paul LePage">Paul LePage</a>. The state's two members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a> are Democrat <a href="/wiki/Chellie_Pingree" title="Chellie Pingree">Chellie Pingree</a> and Republican <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Poliquin" title="Bruce Poliquin">Bruce Poliquin</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipalities">Municipalities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Municipalities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organized_municipalities">Organized municipalities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Organized municipalities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An organized municipality has a form of elected local government which administers and provides local services, keeps records, collects licensing fees, and can pass locally binding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipal_ordinance" title="Municipal ordinance">ordinances</a>, among other responsibilities of self-government. The governmental format of most organized towns and <a href="/wiki/Plantation_(Maine)" title="Plantation (Maine)">plantations</a> is the town meeting, while the format of most cities is the council-manager form. As of 2013 the organized municipalities of Maine consist of 23 <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Maine" title="List of cities in Maine">cities</a>, 431 <a href="/wiki/List_of_towns_in_Maine" title="List of towns in Maine">towns</a>, and 34 <a href="/wiki/List_of_plantations_in_Maine" title="List of plantations in Maine">plantations</a>. Collectively these 488 organized municipalities cover less than half of the state's territory. Maine also has 3 Reservations: <a href="/wiki/Penobscot_Indian_Island_Reservation" title="Penobscot Indian Island Reservation">Indian Island</a>, Indian Township Reservation, and Pleasant Point Indian Reservation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>The largest municipality in Maine, by population, is the city of <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Maine" title="Portland, Maine">Portland</a> (pop. 66,318).</li>
<li>The smallest city by population is <a href="/wiki/Eastport,_Maine" title="Eastport, Maine">Eastport</a> (pop. 1,331).</li>
<li>The largest town by population is <a href="/wiki/Brunswick,_Maine" title="Brunswick, Maine">Brunswick</a> (pop. 20,278).</li>
<li>The smallest town by population is <a href="/wiki/Frye_Island,_Maine" title="Frye Island, Maine">Frye Island</a>, a resort town which reported zero year-round population in the 2000 Census; one plantation, <a href="/wiki/Glenwood_Plantation,_Maine" title="Glenwood Plantation, Maine">Glenwood Plantation, Maine</a>, also reported a permanent population of zero.</li>
<li>In the 2000 census, the smallest town aside from Frye Island was <a href="/wiki/Centerville,_Maine" title="Centerville, Maine">Centerville</a> with a population of 26, but since that census, Centerville voted to disincorporate and therefore is no longer a town. The next smallest town with a population listed in that census is <a href="/wiki/Beddington,_Maine" title="Beddington, Maine">Beddington</a> (pop. 50 at the 2010 census).</li>
<li>The largest municipality by land area is the town of <a href="/wiki/Allagash,_Maine" title="Allagash, Maine">Allagash</a>, at 128 square miles (332 km<sup>2</sup>).</li>
<li>The smallest municipality by land area is the plantation of <a href="/wiki/Monhegan,_Maine" title="Monhegan, Maine">Monhegan Island</a>, at 0.86 square miles (2.2 km<sup>2</sup>). The smallest municipality by area that is not an island is <a href="/wiki/Randolph,_Maine" title="Randolph, Maine">Randolph</a>, at 2.23 square miles (6 km<sup>2</sup>).</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unorganized_territory">Unorganized territory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Unorganized territory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Unorganized_territory" title="Unorganized territory">Unorganized territory</a> has no local government. Administration, services, licensing, and ordinances are handled by the state government. The unorganized territory of Maine consists of over 400 townships (towns are incorporated, townships are unincorporated), plus many coastal islands that do not lie within any municipal bounds. The UT land area is slightly over one half the entire area of the State of Maine. Year-round residents in the UT number approximately 9,000, about 1.3% of the state's total population, with many more people residing only seasonally within the UT. Only four of <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Maine" title="List of counties in Maine">Maine's sixteen counties</a> (Androscoggin, Cumberland, Waldo and York) are entirely incorporated, although a few others are nearly so, and most of the unincorporated area is in the vast and sparsely populated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maine_North_Woods" title="Maine North Woods">Great North Woods of Maine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>

<p>Throughout Maine, many municipalities, although each separate governmental entities, nevertheless form portions of a much larger population base. There are many such population clusters throughout Maine, but some examples from the municipalities appearing in the above listing are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Portland, South Portland, Cape Elizabeth, Westbrook, Scarborough, and Falmouth</li>
<li>Lewiston and Auburn</li>
<li>Bangor, Orono, Brewer, Old Town, and Hampden</li>
<li>Biddeford, Saco and Old Orchard Beach</li>
<li>Brunswick and Topsham</li>
<li>Waterville, Winslow, Fairfield, and Oakland</li>
<li>Presque Isle and Caribou<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Maine" title="List of colleges and universities in Maine">List of colleges and universities in Maine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Maine" title="Education in Maine">Education in Maine</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_high_schools_in_Maine" title="List of high schools in Maine">List of high schools in Maine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_school_districts_in_Maine" title="List of school districts in Maine">List of school districts in Maine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:184px;max-width:184px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">

</div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Bates_College" title="Bates College">Bates College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bowdoin_College" title="Bowdoin College">Bowdoin College</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lewiston,_Maine" title="Lewiston, Maine">Lewiston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brunswick,_Maine" title="Brunswick, Maine">Brunswick</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are thirty institutions of <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher learning</a> in Maine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> These institutions include the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maine" title="University of Maine">University of Maine</a>, which is the oldest, largest and only <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">research university</a> in the state. UMaine was founded in 1865 and is the state's only <a href="/wiki/Land_grant" title="Land grant">land grant</a> and sea grant college. The University of Maine is located in the town of <a href="/wiki/Orono,_Maine" title="Orono, Maine">Orono</a> and is the flagship of Maine. There are also branch campuses in <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maine_at_Augusta" title="University of Maine at Augusta">Augusta</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maine_at_Farmington" title="University of Maine at Farmington">Farmington</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maine_at_Fort_Kent" title="University of Maine at Fort Kent">Fort Kent</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maine_at_Machias" title="University of Maine at Machias">Machias</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maine_at_Presque_Isle" title="University of Maine at Presque Isle">Presque Isle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bowdoin_College" title="Bowdoin College">Bowdoin College</a> is a liberal arts college founded in 1794 in <a href="/wiki/Brunswick,_Maine" title="Brunswick, Maine">Brunswick</a>, making it the oldest institution of higher learning in the state. <a href="/wiki/Colby_College" title="Colby College">Colby College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Waterville,_Maine" title="Waterville, Maine">Waterville</a> was founded in 1813 making it the second oldest college in Maine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bates_College" title="Bates College">Bates College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lewiston,_Maine" title="Lewiston, Maine">Lewiston</a> was founded in 1855 making it the third oldest institution in the state and the oldest <a href="/wiki/Mixed-sex_education" title="Mixed-sex education">coeducational</a> college in <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:31_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-:31-91">[91]</a></sup> The three colleges collectively form the <a href="/wiki/Colby-Bates-Bowdoin_Consortium" title="Colby-Bates-Bowdoin Consortium">Colby-Bates-Bowdoin Consortium</a> and are ranked among the best colleges in the United States; often placing in the top 10% of all liberal arts colleges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:201px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UMaine_StevensHall.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/UMaine_StevensHall.jpg/199px-UMaine_StevensHall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/UMaine_StevensHall.jpg/299px-UMaine_StevensHall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/UMaine_StevensHall.jpg/398px-UMaine_StevensHall.jpg 2x" width="199"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UMaine_StevensHall.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Stevens Hall at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maine" title="University of Maine">University of Maine</a> in <a href="/wiki/Orono,_Maine" title="Orono, Maine">Orono</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Maine's per-student public expenditure for elementary and secondary schools was 21st in the nation in 2012, at $12,344.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>The collegiate system of Maine also includes numerous <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Classification_of_Institutions_of_Higher_Education" title="Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education">baccalaureate</a> colleges such as: the <a href="/wiki/Maine_Maritime_Academy" title="Maine Maritime Academy">Maine Maritime Academcy</a> (MMA), <a href="/wiki/Unity_College_(Maine)" title="Unity College (Maine)">Unity College</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_College" title="Thomas College">Thomas College</a>. There is only one medical school in the state, (<a href="/wiki/University_of_New_England_(United_States)" title="University of New England (United States)">University of New England</a>'s <a href="/wiki/University_of_New_England_College_of_Osteopathic_Medicine" title="University of New England College of Osteopathic Medicine">College of Osteopathic Medicine</a>) and only one law school (The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maine_School_of_Law" title="University of Maine School of Law">University of Maine School of Law</a>).</p>
<p>Private schools in Maine are funded independently of the state and its furthered domains. Private schools are less common than public schools. A large number of private elementary schools with under 20 students exist, but most private high schools in Maine can be described as "semi-private."</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Maine_in_popular_culture" title="Maine in popular culture">Maine in popular culture</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Maine" title="List of people from Maine">List of people from Maine</a></div>
<p>A citizen of Maine is known as a "Mainer",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mainer_definition_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-mainer_definition-3">[3]</a></sup> though the term is often reserved for those whose roots in Maine go back at least three generations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> The term "Downeaster" may be applied to residents of the northeast coast of the state. The term "Mainiac" is considered by some to be derogatory, but embraced with pride by others,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> and is used for a variety of organizations and for events such as the YMCA Mainiac Sprint Triathlon &amp; Duathlon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
